           Channels for Neutron-Induced Reaction on 48Ti for En   1416200100004 
           = 1 to 200 MeV                                         1416200100005 
AUTHOR     (D.Dashdorj,G.E.Mitchell,J.A.Becker,U.Agvaanluvsan,    1416200100006 
           L.A.Bernstein,W.Younes,P.E.Garrett,M.B.Chadwick,       1416200100007 
           M.Devlin,N.Fotiades,T.Kawano,R.O.Nelson)               1416200100008 
INSTITUTE  (1USALRL,1USANCS,1USATNL,1CANGUE,1USALAS)              1416200100009 
REFERENCE  (J,NSE,157,65,2007)                                    1416200100010 
FACILITY   (LINAC,1USALAS)Weapons Neutron Research facility       1416200100011 
           WNR at the Los Alamos Neutron Science Center LANSCE    1416200100012 
INC-SOURCE (SPALL) Neutrons are produced by bombarding a natural  1416200100013 
           tungsten target with the 800-MeV pulsed proton beam    1416200100014 
           from the LANSCE linac. Neutrons with energies ranging  1416200100015 
           from a few keV to nearly 800 MeV are produced.         1416200100016 
           Beam-hardening material ~1.5 cm of lead was placed     1416200100017 
           in the neutron flight path, and charged particles      1416200100018 
           were swept from the flight line by permanent magnets   1416200100019 
SAMPLE     3.3 g of TiO2 enriched to 99.81% 48Ti in the form of   1416200100020 
           a 2.4-cm-diam disk                                     1416200100021 
DETECTOR   (HPGE)The gamma rays were detected with the GEANIE     1416200100022 
           spectrometer, located 20.34 m from the neutron         1416200100023 
           source on the 60-deg right flight path.                1416200100024 
           The GEANIE spectrometer consisted of 11                1416200100025 
           planar and fifteen ~20% to 25% HPGe coaxial            1416200100026 
           detectors. All of the planar detectors and 9 of the    1416200100027 
           coaxial detectors were equipped with Compton           1416200100028 
           suppression shields. The detectors were situated at    1416200100029 
           a distance of 14 cm from the the scattering sample     1416200100030 
METHOD     (TOF,GSPEC) The detection time of gamma rays           1416200100031 
           produced by neutrons interacting with the sample was   1416200100032 
           used to calculate the TOF of the neutrons relative     1416200100033 
           to the micropulse time, measured by g-flash detection. 1416200100034 
MONITOR    Fission chamber with 235,238U foils, located 2 m       1416200100035 
           upstream from the GEANIE spectrometer. Fission         1416200100036 
           chamber events were used to determine the neutron flux.1416200100037 
ERR-ANALYS (DATA-ERR) No Information                              1416200100038
